To know she hasn’t lost her completely, even after all the insults she threw at her. Even after asking her to leave her alone. To know that if she wanted - Rio would still be hers - and she would…right?

It’s that curiosity (or maybe masochism) that drives Agatha to find a back hallway, the one leading toward the bathrooms. She plants her back against the wall and unlocks her phone. Her thumb has to scroll too far through her recent calls to find Rio’s number. 

She can barely hear the other line over the noise of the music of the bar - bad christmas music mixed with an obnoxious amount of chatter. Plus the swimming in her brain from the multiple tequila shots doesn’t help. 

She presses call. 

The line rings once. Twice. 

She hears someone pick up but doesn’t hear a hello.

Instead, she hears the faint jumble of voices and laughter in the background. 

“Hello?” Agatha says into the speaker. 

No response. 

“Rio?” she tries again, yelling louder into the speaker. “Can you hear me?” 

She pulls the phone from her ear to check the screen. It’s Rio’s number, no mistake there. She presses the phone back to her ear but only hears mumbled voices - the noise of the bar too loud. She sinks further back into the hallway, the music fading and tries to make out what the conversation on the other end is saying. 

A woman’s voice. Not Rio’s. Then a soft giggle.  

“Who knew you were so funny,” the woman says, her tone light and teasing. 

Agatha’s stomach drops. She holds her breath as if it is going to help her hear better. 

“Hey babe?” the voice calls again, muffled now, as if turned toward someone else. 

She hears Rio murmuring in response, but she can’t make out the words. 

Suddenly the voice is much closer, almost next to the phone. “Looks like your phone butt dialed someone.” 

More incoherent words. 

“Hello?” comes the female voice through the line. It’s soft, sultry like butter. And far too cheerful. “Sorry,” comes a laugh, “Rio is unavailable right now.” 

Agatha says nothing. 

“Are you there?” Another giggle. “I can hear you breathing.” 

Agatha covers her mouth, swallowing hard. She doesn’t dare move a muscle. She just listens. 

“I don’t know,” the woman says in the background. “It said ‘Agatha.’” 

Then the line goes dead. 

Agatha freezes. The phone still pressed to her ear, hand covering her mouth. Her pulse is racing so loudly she can hear it in her ears. 

She glances down at her phone screen like it might light up again. Like Rio might call her back and explain. 

But her phone stays dark. 

The ache starts immediately in her chest, blooming outwards until it’s slithering down her arms to her fingertips where they tighten around her phone. She slides down the wall until she’s sitting on the dirty bar floor, legs curled up to her chest. 

She should move. She should stand up. The floor is filthy, covered in years of grime and spilled beer.

Maybe this is what she deserves. 

For getting involved with an attending. For thinking she could rewrite the outcome of her carefully planned life. For pushing Rio away every single time she tried to get close. 

Agatha tips her head back against the wall and stares up at the ceiling. At least that motion keeps the tears from spilling, holding them where they burn most, behind her eyes.

She isn’t sure how long she sits there like that. Eventually Billy comes to find her, his eyes darting around the hallway until they land on her. 

“Oh girl,” He stands above her with his hands on his hips. “Tell me you are not sitting on a bar floor.” 

“I’m not sitting on a bar floor.”

“You are,” he says flatly. “And it’s disgusting.” He reaches his hand out to help her up, grimacing. “I take it things didn’t go well?” 

Agatha lets him pull her to her feet. “She’s not alone,” she says dryly. Billy wipes his hands on his pants, like Agatha is now as dirty as the floor beneath her. 

“That could mean anything,” Billy tries to reassure her as he leads her back to the table. “It’s Christmas, maybe she’s having a family dinner.” 

“With another woman? Just the two of them?” Agatha lifts an eyebrow. 

Alice, already watching from their table, visibly cringes. 

Billy looks sad for her. “Oh,” he mutters. “Well in that case,” he starts flagging down the bartender. “Another round.” 

—

And old fashioned.

A manhattan.

A vodka tonic.

Lemon drop shots. 

Agatha orders it all. Drink after drink hits her lips, each other blurring the edges a little more. None take away the ache Rio has left behind. 

Twice Billy tries to stop her. And once Alice does, although her attempt barely counts - After a minute, she gives up, muttering about not wanting to play babysitter on Christmas. She leaves just Billy and Agatha at the bar. 

“You know what we should do?” Agatha slurs, swaying slightly on her stool. 

“Go home?” Billy suggests. “Sleep it off?”

Agatha groans. “Noooooo. Body shots!” 

Billy exhales loudly. “I know you are sad and everything. But you aren’t really my type, sweetie.” He’s clearly annoyed. Agatha can feel it. But she doesn’t care. 

“Party pooper,” Agatha gives a fake pout. “I wasn’t talking about you anyway.” She grabs his hand and tugs him toward the small dance floor where the strobe lights now flash. They weave in between the bodies, pulsing, sweating, grinding with the music. 

She throws her hands back over her head, feeling the music and booze coursing through her veins. With every breath, every flash of the lights, she sees Rio in her mind. 

Sitting on the couch with some faceless woman. Her hand on her leg. Her hands in her hair. Leaning toward her. Her face coming closer to her lips. 

She slams her eyes shut. 

When she opens them again, she scans the dance floor - a few women dancing with boyfriends, some standing at the edge of the dance floor.

Then she spots her. Red head, slightly shorter than her, her eyeliner thick against her green eyes. 

Her thumbs are hooked into her jean pockets, a beer bottle hanging precariously between her fingers. She makes eye contact with Agatha, bringing the bottle slowly to her lips as she watches her. 

Bingo.

Agatha tries to walk toward her, her heels suddenly too high where the dance floor transitions to the wood floor of the bar. She stumbles slightly, reaching out to catch herself. But the woman steps forward, arms coming up under Agatha’s to steady her. 

The grip is firm across Agatha’s back as she stands up.

“You okay there, dizzy girl?” The woman muses, a slight laughter to her tone.

“Better now,” Agatha sways slightly, but lets herself be held. “Or maybe I just like falling for strangers.”

The redhead laughs, “Oh my, that was cheesy.”

Agatha leans forward toward her. She smells like cheap vanilla perfume and drugstore shampoo. Doesn’t matter. Another drink will mute the smell enough, just for one night. 

“But it still worked,” Agatha’s confidence oozes through, even in her drunken state. 

“That it did,” the redhead purrs. “What’s your name?”

“Doesn’t matter,” Agatha says, words slurring slightly. She looks away from her, not quite meeting her eyes. 

“I’m…”

“Doesn’t matter,” Agatha cuts her off. “You want to do this or not?” 

“That depends,” the woman says, fingers now wrapping around Agatha’s arms, pressing inward. “What did you have in mind?” 

Agatha laughs, a sound that’s too loud, too hollow. “Slow down there, tiger. Let’s go to the bar.” 

The woman frowns slightly. ”That’s it? Just going to buy me a drink?” 

Agatha nods toward the counter. “After you, superstar.” She teases. “I’ll make it worth your trouble.” She’s drunk enough that her judgement is foggy, bold enough that she doesn’t care. 

Billy, somewhere across the room, groans audibly. “Oh, hell,” she hears him mutter, but she’s already moving to the corner of the bar. She climbs on top, laying down and pulling up her top. The bartender merely rolls his eyes, not willing to fight more drunken patrons at this hour. 

The redhead follows, laughing as she slides between Agatha’s legs, lime in hand. She licks along her skin creating a line for the salt. Then pours a shot into her belly button.    

It’s messy. Some might see it as sexy. The woman’s mouth is warm against her stomach.

But Agatha feels nothing.

Her head tilts back, eyes fixed on the spinning lights above. She imagines Rio’s face instead - the way she looks when she’s annoyed, or when she laughs at something stupid Agatha says. For a brief, torturous second, she can almost smell her perfume over the tequila and smoke.

Then the woman’s voice cuts through the noise. “You okay?”

Agatha blinks down at her, swallowing hard. “Yeah,” she lies, voice rough. “Never better.”

Billy’s watching from the edge of the bar now, arms crossed, expression unreadable. He doesn’t stop her. He knows it wouldn’t matter.

Because Agatha isn’t trying to have fun. She’s trying to forget.

When she climbs down from the bar, the redhead is on her, caging her in against the worn wood. 

When she kisses Agatha, it’s all wrong. Her lips feel too thin, too tentative. 

Agatha isn’t melting into the arms of some stranger like she wanted to. She isn’t forgetting Rio. No, she’s standing here with the redhead’s tongue in her mouth, her hands gripping Agatha’s hips - and she’s comparing her. 

“Bathroom? Or my place?” The stranger purrs, her fingers now tracing the lace pattern along Agatha’s stomach. 

“Actually, I’m good,” Agatha plucks the woman’s fingers away from her stomach like she’s picking up a bug. “Thanks though.” She wipes her lips with the back of her hand, trying to erase any trace of the redhead. 

She slithers out of her arms, stepping away from the bar. Then starts looking for Billy. 

“Bitch,” she hears the woman growl behind her. 

“Feel better?” Billy asks as she approaches him. 

“No,” Agatha grunts. 

Billy doesn’t say anything for a while but just leads her to a corner booth, tucked away from the main bar. She follows him without protest, shoulders sagging slightly - out of shame or exhaustion - she isn’t sure which. 

She’s tempted to order another drink. To reach the point of blacking out until she can’t remember her own name. But Billy is sliding a glass of water in front of her and even though she rolls her eyes at him, she takes a sip. 

Her head tips back until it’s resting against the wall. The crowd feels too loud now, the music too harsh. Billy folds his arms as he leans back, watching her. “You done trying to self destruct for the night?”

Agatha doesn’t remove her head from the wall, she just closes her eyes. “That obvious?” 

“You’re sitting in a bar on Christmas letting strangers do shots off of you.”

“Hey, you’re here too!” Agatha shoots back.

“But I’m like an emotional support animal.” Billy laughs quietly. “And a medical alert dog. Someone has to make sure you don’t die.”

Agatha finally lifts her head, but only to roll her eyes at him. 

“You really should call it a night.” He warns, his tone now more serious. 

Agatha nods, but she doesn’t move. Her head rests back again, eyes closing to try to stop the spinning that is now building. “Just five more minutes,” she mutters. 

“Fine,” Billy sighs. “But if you start crying, I’m dragging you out of here.”

“Moi?” Agatha fakes exacerbation. “Never.”

—

Agatha’s head is swimming. It is well past 2am now, the bar has since closed. 

She lied to Billy. Outside the bar, the cold nipping at their skin, she ordered an Uber. As they waited for it, she promised she was heading straight to her mom’s house. But the address she plugged in was one she saved months ago - Rio’s.

Now as the Uber rounds another corner, Agatha glances down at her phone’s GPS. Five minutes until her arrival. She swallows hard, the saliva thick in her throat, the nausea settling into her stomach. She can keep it down. At least long enough to avoid the cleaning fee from vomiting in the car.  

Her stomach turns again. She tells herself it’s the copious amounts of alcohol - mixing tequila, vodka and whatever else she consumed in the last few hours and not the thought of what she’s about to do. Not the confrontation she hasn’t planned out. 

Finally, the car stops in front of Rio’s house. She can see a few lights on and Rio’s car in the driveway. Plus another, one she doesn’t recognize.  

She opens the car door and practically tumbles out. The Uber lingers for only a second, long enough for her to close the door and step onto the sidewalk, before it rolls away and leaves her standing alone. 

Agatha stands there for a long moment, swaying slightly. She stares at the house, seeing the warm light spill through the blinds. A shadow of someone crosses by the window. 

Her throat tightens. The nausea surges again. She doubles over, clutching her stomach as she vomits onto the curb. The sound is raw, humiliating. When it’s done, she wipes her mouth with the back of her hand. 

Her eyes fix on the window again, watching, waiting. Just as she builds up the courage to start walking toward the door, the light flickers off. 

The house goes dark. 

—

 

Chapter 19: Surrender

Chapter Notes

I proofread this at 3am with only 1.5 hours of sleep under my belt. If you see an error - no you don't.
The opener of this chapter was an idea from @SpiralSlide

See the end of the chapter for more notes



Last time on CBAGG: 

Agatha stands there for a long moment, swaying slightly. She stares at the house, seeing the warm light spill through the blinds. A shadow of someone crosses by the window. 

Her throat tightens. The nausea surges again. She doubles over, clutching her stomach as she vomits onto the curb. The sound is raw, humiliating. When it’s done, she wipes her mouth with the back of her hand. 

Her eyes fix on the window again, watching, waiting. Just as she builds up the courage to start walking toward the door, the light flickers off. 

—

Agatha sighs, debating just turning around again and ordering another Uber. Her eyes flick up to Rio’s porch, the only light still illuminated at the house. 

There is a man standing there.

He’s definitely there. Just standing. Watching her.

He’s got on some red jacket, dressed up for Christmas no doubt. He even has on a stupid Santa hat, although it’s a bit sideways. 

Maybe he’s keeping watch while Rio’s inside, fucking her new girlfriend. 

Agatha starts up the walkway, heels crunching through the thin crust of snow. Her fists ball at her sides, fury starting to rise within her. He doesn’t move as she gets closer. He just stares, silent and unbothered by her presence. 

“Who the hell are you?” she calls, stomping up the steps. 

He doesn’t reply, he just stares at her again with a ridiculous smile plastered on his face.

“Hey!” She shouts, getting closer now. “I’m talking to you.” Her voice slurs at the edges. 

He only smiles at her. 

Agatha marches right up to him, her nose centimeters from his. “God you are even uglier than Ralph.” She settles back on her heels. “He’s my fake fiancé. Wait…” she hiccups. “That’s not right.”

She has to think for a second, swaying as she does. “He’s a real fiancé. He might be trapped in this too. Or maybe he really likes me.”

A beat. 

“Oh that’s going to make me vomit again.” She gags at her own words. 

She’s met with silence.

“Fucking say something!” She screams. 

He doesn’t. 

So she shoves him. Hard. 

He teeters sideways, then crashes backward with a hollow thud. 

Agatha stumbles too, catching her leg on part of the patio couch and landing squarely on her ass along the cushions. 

The front door flies open. “What the hell!” Rio stands there barefoot, wearing cream oversized sweatpants and a black long-sleeve top. Her eyes widen as she looks between the man on the floor and Agatha, plastered sideways on the couch. 

“You’re welcome,” Agatha grins up at Rio.

“For breaking my decor?”

“I fought him,” Agatha gives a lopsided smile. “For you.”

“He’s plastic, Agatha.”

Agatha blinks, rubbing her eyes against the harsh light of the porch. The man comes more into focus now from his place on the floor. 

A plastic Santa. 

Shit.

“Sorry ‘bout that,” Agatha chuckles a bit. 

“Jesus,” Rio moans, scrubbing the hand over her face. “Are you drunk? Again?”

She steps forward and offers her hand to pull Agatha up from the porch couch. 

“You realize every time you show up on my porch, you are drunk? If I had a nickel…” Rio starts. 

“Then you would have two nickels!” Agatha beams like she’s cracked some kind of code. 

Rio sighs. “How much did you have to drink?” 

Agatha starts counting on her fingers. “One, two…my fair share.” She shrugs. 

Before Rio can respond, Agatha suddenly lurches toward the railing and vomits over the side. The sound of liquid splashing onto the ground can be heard.

“Let’s just get you inside,” Rio says calmly, holding her arm out to help her walk. 

“Why are you so nice to me?” Agatha whines as she threads her arm through Rio’s. Then, she freezes in the doorway, gasping. “Oh my god. Wait.” Her voice drops to a dramatic stage whisper. “Won’t your girlfriend find out I’m here?”

“What?” Rio sounds genuinely confused, dropping her arm as they step inside. “The phone call,” she concludes on her own. 

“Yeah. The phone call,” Agatha slurs, nodding. 

“Sorry, you heard that.”

Agatha stops. Her hand shoots out to grip the counter, steadying herself. Because even in her drunken state, she has a moment of clarity. Rio didn’t apologize for the phone call. She didn’t explain. She didn’t say she was sorry for what Agatha heard - only sorry that she heard it. 

She feels the bile rising in her throat again. 

She must have gone pale because suddenly Rio is at her side, thrusting a small trash can into her hands. 

Agatha retches, dry heaving slightly, but no further liquid comes out. Instead she feels Rio’s warm hand is at her back, rubbing small circles. 

“I’m fine,” Agatha hisses back, even as she clutches the trash can and staggers toward the couch. 

Unceremoniously, she plops down, her legs dangling off the edge. 

Agatha closes her eyes, waiting for the spinning to stop. Then she feels it, the warm hands again, this time at her ankles, undoing the buckles of her heels. Her shoes slide off and hee feet are gently lifted onto the couch. 

She hears the shuffle of feet on the carpet and assumes Rio is leaving her alone to sleep it off. 

“Zofran,” Rio says suddenly. Agatha isn’t sure if it’s been a minute or an hour. She opens one eye to see Rio standing over her with a small dissolvable tablet. 

“Open,” Rio instructs. 

Agatha’s mouth drops open and Rio drops the pill in. Agatha lets her head sink back into the pillow. 

A finger pokes her shoulder again, waking her. 

“Water,” Rio guides the glass to Agatha’s mouth as she sits up slightly. She takes a few large gulps then settles into the pillow once more. 

Then she feels a blanket being dragged up over her, tucked gently into her sides.

“Why are you helping me?” She mumbles. 

Rio’s back is turned, rummaging through a cabinet. She turns around with an armful of plastic tubing and supplies. 

“So you don’t die on my couch,” Rio sticks her tongue in her cheek. She kneels beside the couch, laying everything out on the coffee table. She starts opening packages, lining up supplies in a neat line. 

“Arm please,” she sticks her hand out. As Agatha rests her arm in Rio’s hand, she presses along her inner elbow for a vein. A bright orange tourniquet gets snapped around her arm. 

Only now does Agatha really notice what’s on the table - tubing, bandages, needles and a large bag of saline. 

“You’re giving me an IV?”

“Honey, trust me. You need it.” 

“Where did you even get the supplies?” She hiccups softly. 

“Hospital supply closet. Expired. They throw them out anyway.” 

“Is this even safe?”

“Shut up and close your eyes,” Rio warns. “Big poke,” she says in a pandering voice. 

Agatha winces as the needle slides in her arm. 

Rio works silently, securing the line to Agatha’s arm with a small clear bandage. She hooks up the IV tubing, placing the bag of fluids on the couch behind Agatha’s head. 

Agatha’s eyes close again, feeling drowsy, like her limbs are too heavy for her body - a mixture of booze and fatigue. She feels Rio’s hand ghost across her forehead, sweeping back a loose strand of hair. 

Rio must think she’s asleep. Otherwise she wouldn’t be touching her like that. 

“You know I love you, right?” Agatha murmurs. 

Rio stills. Her hand hovers a moment longer - then slips away. 

“You’re drunk,” Rio murmurs.

Agatha hiccups, blinking up at her. “I am,” she admits. “But that’s why I came over. Why I called. To tell you that.” 

“Oh,” Rio breathes. She settles onto the floor again, her back resting against the couch next to Agatha’s head. She doesn’t say more, almost like she’s letting the words soak through her. 

Agatha closes her eyes, slowly. Her breathing evens out, soft puffs of air drifting toward Rio until she’s fully asleep.

Rio leans her head back, letting her hair rest next to Agatha’s forehead. 

“I wish that was true,” Rio whispers to no one. 

—

Agatha can hear voices. Two females ones. Rio’s she recognizes instantly, the other feels vaguely familiar but she can’t place it. 

She keeps her eyes closed from her place on the couch, faking sleep for a while longer as she focuses on the other voice. 

It’s hard to think clearly with the pounding in her head. 

“She’s really pretty, Rio,” she hears the other woman say. 

“I know,” Rio sighs. “Don’t tell her that. I don’t need it going to her head,” she chuckles. 

Agatha hears Rio tell her goodbye. Then the sound of footsteps and the soft click of the front door. 

“You can open your eyes now Agatha,” Rio calls from across the room, probably in the kitchen. “You don’t have to fake sleep anymore.”

Agatha rubs her eyes and stretches, prolonging the ruse just a little bit longer. She can smell the scent of coffee now drifting in from the kitchen. 

Rio comes back with a steaming mug in her hand and offers it to Agatha as she sits up. 

As Agatha reaches out, she notices the small bandage across her inner elbow. She furrows her brow. 

“When did I get injured?” She questions, looking at Rio. 

“You don’t remember?” Rio asks.

Agatha shakes her head. “I remember the bar. Billy was there. And a lot of drinks. I think there was a dance floor.” She shrugs. “Did you come get me?” 

“You showed up,” Rio explains. “Destroyed my plastic Santa. He was vintage by the way.” 

“Shit,” Agatha drops her head in her hands. “I’m sorry. For all of it. I didn’t do anything else embarrassing, did it?”

“No, that was it,” Rio lies. “You came in and passed out on the couch. I gave you some IV fluids.” She nods at the bandage. 

“And,” Agatha glances between them. “Nothing else happened?”

“Agatha,” Rio’s tone turns serious. “I would never take advantage of you like that in a drunken state.” 

“I know,” Agatha admits, a small smile tugging at her lips. “But I can get pretty flirty when I’m drunk.”

“And sentimental,” Rio adds under her breath. 

“What?”

“Nothing,” she says quickly.

Agatha rises from the couch, mug in hand as she looks around the living room.

She pauses in one corner where there is a round table covered in a small red sheet with a Christmas tree on top.

“You got a tiny Christmas tree.”

“Yeah,” Rio hesitates. 

“It doesn’t have any ornaments.”

“Well I bought it a while ago. I had hoped we could…” Rio shakes her head. “You know what, nevermind.”

The silence stretches between them, Agatha’s fingers gently brushing along the plastic branches. 

Finally Rio speaks up, “I should explain this morning.” 

Agatha stiffens, her shoulders tightening. “No need. You have your life, I have mine.” She turns back toward Rio, setting the coffee cup on the table before smoothing out her pants. “I should get going anyway, thank you for taking care of me.” She bends down and grabs her shoes, not bothering to put them on. “Again, sorry I showed up. And broke your plastic thing. I can pay for it…really…and…”

“Agatha, that was my cousin,” Rio cuts her off. 

“The Santa?” Agatha jokes. Rio huffs. 

“The woman here last night. And this morning. That was my cousin. I haven’t seen her in years. She came into town for Christmas. We had dinner with my family and I have an extra bedroom, so she stayed here for the night.”

“You aren’t dating someone,” Agatha says almost in disbelief. 

“Nope,” Rio adds. “When you said you wanted more time, I took you seriously. I waited. And then the gala - you told me to stop pursuing you. And I did. But that doesn’t mean I started pursuing other people.”

Agatha swallows, her heart racing. “You waited for me.”

“I did,” Rio says softly, almost a whisper. 

Agatha drops her shoes onto the floor and takes three giant strides toward Rio. She grabs the side of her face, leans in, kissing her tentatively. Her lips press into Rio’s until she slowly opens her mouth. 

It’s light, fleeting - reassurance and relief. 

Then Rio winces a bit as she slowly pulls back.

“I’m sorry,” Agatha starts rushing, the words coming quickly. “I shouldn’t have assumed, just because you said…”

“It’s not that,” Rio starts. “You threw up a lot last night.”

Agatha covers her mouth, realizing. “Still have my toothbrush?” She asks. 

“Yeah. It’s….” She gestures toward the bathroom. 

Agatha smiles. “Be right back.” 

Rio sighs. The whole morning is going better than she expected. It’s not quite the love confession of last night, but at least Agatha is sober and telling the truth. At least they aren’t fighting. Or pushing each other away. 

A firm knock on the door interrupts her thoughts. 

Rio peers through the peep hole to see two uniformed male police officers staring back at her. 

Evanora stands next to them, bundled in an oversized coat with a handkerchief in her hand. 

For fuck’s sake. 

“Can I help you?” Rio opens the door just wide enough to stick her head out. 

“We have reports of a missing person.” 

“My baby!” Evanora wails, dabbing her eyes with the handkerchief. Not a single tear is visible. 

“Do you know the whereabouts of Agatha Harkness?” the taller officer asks. 

“She’s a grown adult,” Rio growls in a low voice. “She came over voluntarily,” 

“Rio?” Agatha’s voice comes from behind her. “What’s the matter?” 

“Is that her, ma’am?” The officer leans forward, trying to see past her. 

Rio opens the door wider until Agatha is visible next to her. She’s scrubbed her face free of her makeup but is still in her club clothes from last night, feet bare. 

“Oh my goodness! There she is!” Evanora chokes out. “Come here darling!” She exclaims as she reaches her arms out. 

Agatha doesn’t move, “Good lord.” She rolls her eyes at the acting display in front of her. “Let me get my stuff,” she deadpans. 

Rio’s jaw clenches. “You don’t have to go with her,” Rio points out. 

Agatha turns, grabbing her shoes before slipping them on. She squeezes Rio’s arm as she passes, trying to reassure her. 

“It’s just easier this way. Don’t worry about me.” she whispers. “Let’s not cause a scene,” she brushes it off like it’s an everyday occurrence. 

Evanora moves in instantly, blocking a path from Rio to Agatha. “I’d like to press charges,” she scowls at the officers. 

“For what exactly?” 

“Child endangerment. Kidnapping.” 

“She’s not a minor, ma’am,” the officer replies flatly. “She appears unharmed.”

“I’m the one who came over here, Mother.”

Evanora’s eyes flare, then she balls up the handkerchief and throws it on the porch. She stomps down the stairs off the porch toward her car. 

Despite Rio’s concern, Agatha actually chuckles at the antics, like she’s watching a toddler throw a tantrum. 

“Agatha,” Rio warns one last time as the group starts to leave. “Are you sure?” 

“I’ll call you tonight,” Agatha smiles as she skips down the porch toward the car. 

—

Rio attempts to busy herself for the day. She cleans up the massacred Santa mess, hoses off several spots of vomit from her front porch and sidewalk and clears out the IV tubing from last night. 

Her phone stays glued to her side the entire time. Every notification, every buzz has her reaching for it - hoping to hear from Agatha again. 

But nothing. 

Agatha said she would call her, and she’s trying to give her that space to do so. But as the sun sets, she tells herself that by 8pm, she’s calling her. 

The clock reads 7:32pm when Rio’s phone finally buzzes. 

Made it home - is all the message reads. Flat, no detail. And certainly not a recent event. 

Another message follows seconds later: I’m sorry about all of it. 

Rio isn’t sure what she’s apologizing for - the drunken visit, the Santa, her mother. None of that matters. 

At this moment Rio cares about two things - first and foremost that Agatha is ok; which seems to be the case. 

Second. she really wants to talk about is the drunken confession; the one Rio is sure Agatha doesn’t remember. And the emotional morning and kissing her - now that Rio cares about. 

Her thumbs hover over the screen, typing and retyping the messages a few times to try to phrase it best. 

Finally, she settles on the simplest thing. The important thing is you are okay. 

You worry too much - comes the quick response. 

Can you blame me? You basically live with the devil herself - Rio replies.

The devil has gone back to ignoring me completely while she drinks in her office. So don’t fret tonight, I’m safe in my room :) 

Rio tries to believe her, but something eats at her tonight. She doesn’t know what it is - call it intuition, or maybe paranoia. But something feels off.

Rio keeps her phone on ring tonight. Just in case. 

—

Sure enough, by 3am her phone rings. The noise is too loud, startling her from her sleep. 

Agatha. 

Rio laughs into the speaker as she answers. “I swear to God if you are drunk again and begging to come over…”

Then Rio can hear the sounds of the New Years Eve countdown starting outside the bathroom door. The loud collection of residents starts shouting a countdown as the clock ticks closer to midnight. 

“That’s it,” Rio grinding her hand again, fucking Agatha ruthlessly. “Make a mess of my hand like the filthy girl that you are. All for me.” 

10…

9…

Rio adds a third finger into her without warning, stretching her open. Agatha’s eyes grow wide. 

8…

7…

“I’m close…” Agatha mumbles, barely audible, barely coherent. 

6…

5…

Agatha’s cunt tightens in a brutal clench, one long, ripping wave that knocks the breath out of her. 

4…

3…

Agatha’s hips press into Rio’s hand, firm and fast. 

2…

1…

“Happy New Year!” Erupts from the living room, cheers and laughter leaking into the small bathroom. At the same time, the heat coiling inside Agatha starts to break. Her eyes lock with Rio’s in the mirror. Instinct tells her to look away, to shut her eyes and escape the intensity of that gaze - but she doesn’t. 

The amber eyes staring back at her are unexpectedly soft, warm…and loving. The sight undoes her.

Agatha comes with a muffled cry. Rio’s name tears from her throat, swallowed by the fabric still in her mouth. Rio’s arm reaches around her middle, their eyes still locked as Rio holds her upright through her shutters.  

Agatha is still trembling through the small aftershocks as Rio loosens her grip on her - just enough to give her space to breathe. Her palm stays anchored on her hip, steadying her as the last shivers run through her body. 

She withdraws her fingers then reaches up and gently removes the lace from Agatha’s mouth, brushing her thumb across Agatha’s lips to wipe the dampness away. Agatha slides her dress back down her hips. 

“You still with me?” Rio asks quietly, forehead pressing to the side of Agatha’s head. 

“Barely,” Agatha whispers, leaning back into her. “That was…a lot.”

“I know.” Rio reassures her. “Come here.”

She turns Agatha around gently and pulls her into her chest, wrapping both arms around her. Agatha melts instantly. She buries her face in Rio’s neck, fingers clutching at the fabric of Rio’s vest like an anchor. 

Rio holds her tight, swaying a little, grounding her. Her hands stroke slow circles on Agatha’s back, her voice soft. 

“You’re ok,” she says. “I’m here.”

Agatha’s breath stutters again, this time with relief. She presses a small, shaky kiss to Rio’s shoulder. 

“Don’t let go yet,” Agatha murmurs. 

“Not planning to,” Rio whispers into her hair. 

At those words, Agatha’s whole body settles into Rio’s. Their breathing slowly synchronizes as they hold each other. Then Rio lowers her head, lips brushing the corner of Agatha’s jaw. 

“Happy New Year, Agatha.”

Agatha turns her face toward her, eyes heavy but shining. “Happy New Year, Rio.” 

—

Agatha spots him before he sees her. Ralph is sitting by the window of a small coffee shop, a paper cup in his hand. He’s looking out the window, not toward the door as she walks in. But instead his eye line follows some girl’s ass as she walks by. Figures.

She opens the door, forgoing ordering at the counter and slides into the seat opposite him without a greeting. 

“I’m glad you agreed to meet with me,” Ralph says before offering a sad, but hopeful smile. “I just felt like we should talk.” 

“Honestly, I didn’t really want to,” Agatha leans back, arms crossed as she rolls her eyes. “Rio thought it might be good for me. Growth or some shit.”

Ralph flinches a bit when she mentions Rio’s name. He tries to shake it off, but Agatha can tell he is still uncomfortable. “Did you want something to drink? I’ll buy,” he offers. 

“I don’t plan on staying long,” Agatha reaches for her phone, checking the time before setting it back down on the table. “So what do you want?” Her voice is clipped. 

“Evanora still thinks you’ll marry me. That you’ll come around. Just so you know.”

Agatha rolls her eyes. “And what do you think?” It comes out sarcastic with a scoff. 

He doesn’t answer. He just gives her a pleading look, then looks down as his coffee cup like it might give him more sympathy. 

She almost feels bad for him, the way he looks at her - still hopeful. Like he’s waiting for her to say she changed her mind, like today might give him a different outcome. “Did you really love me?” She asks. 

“I liked you enough that I thought we could make it work and the love would come.”

“It’s not supposed to work like that.”

His jaw tightens, fingers still on his coffee cup. “How would you know? You in love with that woman?” He spits.

Agatha doesn’t flinch. She just considers his words. “Yes,” she says softly. And it feels good. The world does implode around her like a dying star when she says it. It just feels…right. 

Ralph’s face falls. “Does she know?”

“No.” Agatha shakes her head. 

“Why haven’t you told her?”

Agatha lets out a long, loud sigh. “I’m just…I’m not ready yet.” 

He huffs, something bitter behind the sound and narrows his eyes at her. “Seems you are no better off than me with then.” His gaze flicks down to her hands. “You sure you don’t want to give this another try?”

Before she can stop him, he’s reaching out. His fingers brush the back of her left hand, where her engagement ring should be. The touch is light, but Agatha jerks back instantly, like the touch physically burns her. She pulls her hands down under the table to rest on her lap. 

Her eyes sharpen, realization setting in. “What did she offer you?” 

His lips curl, bitterly amused that she caught on so quickly. “A hundred thousand dollars to get you down the aisle,” Ralph shrugs. “Honestly, I don’t know why she cares so much.”

Agatha lets out a dark laugh. “Because she can’t let her black sheep of a daughter ruin her perfect image. What would the hospital donors think? Her church group? No matter how much Evanora hates me, she can’t look like she failed as a mother. She just wants to make sure she looks good.”

“I take it that’s a no then,” Ralph says definitively. 

“More like ‘over my dead body.’”

“I thought you might say something like that.” Ralph exhales before he reaches down, grabbing a folder out of the bag next to him on the floor. A bag Agatha didn’t even notice until this moment. “I didn’t want to have to do this, but you are leaving me no choice.”

He opens the folder to reveal several enlarged photos - Rio and Agatha leaving her apartment. Rio and Agatha driving to the hospital together. All taken at a distance. Like they were being watched.

“So what? These mean nothing. I spend time with her because she helps me study for boards.” Agatha pushes the photos back toward him. 

Ralph throws her a look. Then slides the photos over to reveal the next few - Agatha on Rio’s lap in her car. Kissing her goodbye outside the hospital. And worse, Agatha pressed up against the building, Rio’s hands up her shirt.

Agatha’s throat goes dry. “Shit.”

“Let me just propose something. And don’t answer me yet. Just think about it. We get married, you live your life, secretly. Discreetly.”

Agatha stiffens then covers it by crossing her arms, trying to feign indifference. 

Ralph continues. “We divorce after year, quietly. Your mom stays happy, no ruined image. Just ‘irreconcilable differences.’ No one is the wiser.”

“You think that’s going to work on me?”

“I do,” Ralph grins and this time it’s something more sinister. “I think you want to keep your residency spot. And she wants to keep her job.” His smile widens, no pretense of being nice, just all predatory now. So yeah, I do.” 

Agatha doesn’t respond. Not yet. She slowly gathers the photos in her fingers, tapping them onto the table to gather them in a neat stack. 

“You know what’s wild, Ralph.” Her smile curling into something more sinister. “I used to think you were harmless. Spineless, sure. Eager to please. But harmless.”

Agatha can see him try to muster up enough courage for a comeback. But she shuts it down instantly. 

“Burn them. Frame them. Shove them up your ass for all I care.” She shoves the photos back toward him. 

Ralph bristles, anger starting to bubble up.“You’re in over your head with her, you know that right?”

“Rio or my mother?” Agatha laughs sharply. 

“Evanora will crucify you both.”

Agatha just shakes her head. “You don’t get it. I’m not scared of you. And I’m not scared of her. Not anymore.” Agatha’s eyes drop to the folder of images, Ralph’s hand splayed across the folder protectively. “And yeah,” she swallows. “I love her. And I haven’t told her yet because I want the words to matter. And because for once, I’m choosing the timing of my own damn life.”

With that she stands, grabbing her coat and throwing it over her shoulders. She turns, the material swishing behind her like a cape. 

“And Ralph?” She turns one last time, leaning toward him just enough that he feels her warning. “Next time you try to pick on someone, choose someone who’s actually afraid of losing.”

Then she lifts her middle finger up and stomps out. 

—

 

 

 

 

Chapter 22: Verity

Chapter Notes

This one is going to hurt, but not in the way you expect.

Sorry for the formatting. I’ll fix it when I can get to my computer

TW for graphic depictions of CPR, death and dying.

See the end of the chapter for more notes

 

— 

 

Agatha has been stewing over her encounter with Ralph for days. 

First, she was filled with pure anger. She debated showing up at his house several times, thought about trying to throw a punch (something she’d never done), or kicking him in the groin (something she’s definitely done). 

Then sadness. She tried to pretend she didn’t have tears in her eyes every time she recalled the photos of her and Rio’s private moments being violated.  

Then she started contemplating revenge. She thought of all the ways she could kill Ralph (or Evanora) and make it look like an accident. She was a doctor after all; there are lots of good options - high dose insulin injected between the toes, accidental overdose of a tricyclic antidepressant (which she knew Evanora took), poisoning with death cap mushroom (which Agatha learned from one of Rio’s botany books).  

Ultimately those all felt too risky. 

She has been meaning to tell Rio about it, she really has (the blackmail, not the possible murder). 

But since the NYE party, life has been swallowing them whole. Rio got slammed with a week of nights, Agatha dove headfirst into board prep, and their worlds barely brushed. Passing kisses exchanged at shift change. Feeling each up in hospital hallways. A few exhausted texts. Not nearly enough.

Today she’s going to pull Rio aside and tell her everything - Ralph and Evanora conspiring to blackmail both of them. Today needs to be the day. Agatha can’t take the pressure in her chest any longer. 

She’s sure Rio isn’t going to run, right? Not after how far they’ve come. How much they’ve sacrificed for each other. Not after the way Rio has chosen her, again and again - even when Agatha pushed her away. 

But every time that feeling settles, when Agatha feels like they have their footing on solid ground - it’s like Evanora is suddenly there again - a sniper in the periphery, waiting for the perfect shot. 

Agatha wants to tell Rio she loves her. She’s ready for that too. But in the wake of the photos, she’s worried it will seem more like a Hail Mary than a confession of her feelings. 

So Agatha bites the skin along her thumb nail as she sits next to Rio in the conference room on Monday morning. The entire team is here, so it’s not quite the right place to drop a relationship bomb on her. But still, she can break the ice a bit. 

When Agatha looks over to Rio’s computer screen next to her, she sees her eyes are glued ahead of her. Unmoving. Staring. Rio hasn’t typed for five minutes. 

As she watches her, feelings ready to burst through, she notices something. 

Rio looks wrong.

She’s more distracted than usual. Off-kilter somehow.

Her fingers hover too long over the keyboard. Her jaw flexes. Her eyes keep sweeping the hallway like she’s watching, waiting for something. Agatha has no idea what. 

Agatha watches her for a moment, worry prickling. 

“Rio?” She asks gently, probing.

Rio nearly jumps out of her skin at the intrusion, even though Agatha’s voice was barely above a whisper. 

“You good?” 

Rio’s lips curl into a tight, tense smile. “Yeah,” is all she replies back, the tone too tight. 

“Want to head up to the floors with me?” Agatha asks, hoping to gauge her reaction. 

“Sure…” Rio stands. She seems to pause for a moment, calculating what she needs to bring with her - laptop, coffee and stethoscope.

They walk toward the elevator bank. 

“Are you okay?” Agatha tries. “You seem jumpy.”

“I’m fine,” Rio says, stabbing the elevator button harder than necessary. “Just tired.”

Agatha sucks in a breath before leaving against the back wall of the elevator. Rio says nothing. 

As the elevator hums to life, Agatha’s mind is rattling through their interactions, their texts, trying to find what went wrong. 

Instead of landing on a solution, her stomach just lurches, a nervous pit forming. 

Now her idea to tell Rio she loves her doesn’t feel so brave after all. 

—

Something feels wrong about today. 

Rio notices it the moment she steps through the hospital doors. The air feels heavy with something unspoken. 

Rio can’t name it, but it’s there like an electric hum. The hospital is alive with it, unseen but running through the walls. 

It settles into her bones, bringing an uneasy feeling deep into her chest. 

She feels it again as she gathers her patient list. She glances through the names, nothing unusual stands out. Rio takes a deep, but shaky breath and opens her laptop to click through her charts. 

She keeps searching for the source of the feeling - like her soul can reach out and capture the source of her anxiety. She constantly checks her pager, swearing she felt a vibration that never comes. Her eyes dart to every corner of the hallways like she hears Evanora heading her way, only for there to be no one there. 

Instead, the hospital hums on - the day extremely ordinary. And somehow that makes it worse. 

Agatha doesn’t seem to notice at first. Not when she drops into her seat across the conference room table. Not when she slides Rio an iced coffee she picked up for her before the shift. And certainly not as she winks at Rio from across the conference room table. 

Truth be told, Rio isn’t sure this feeling isn’t about her. Maybe it’s the underlying tension of barely seeing each other for the past week. Or the lack of sex from being too busy. Her sharp, selfish craving to get her alone, beneath her. Maybe it’s something else entirely. 

But Rio doesn’t have the energy to battle it today. She just lets the feeling slowly wash over her, consume her thoughts until she feels like a wallowing ball of sludge - and it’s only 8am.  

Then Agatha starts poking at it - jolting her out of her thoughts and into the present. Rio can tell she’s worried about her, worried about them, and Rio can do nothing to reassure her. 

When Agatha asks if she’s ok, Rio doesn’t know how to answer her - how do you explain that you think your entire day might crumble because you sense it might? It sounds insane to say out loud. 

But then half the day goes by and nothing falls apart. 

Does she still feel like she’s a walking piece of glass, waiting to crack into a million pieces at any moment? Yes. 

Does it take three times as much energy and concentration as usual for Rio to get through her day? Also yes.

And does Agatha stare at her the entire morning, her eyes a mix of concern and what looks like anticipation (for what, Rio has no idea). A resounding yes. 

Still Rio rounds on all her patients, discharges three of them and has time to talk to Chloe in her room.

Chloe is more upbeat than usual, which she’s attributing to the new chemotherapy actually working. 

Rio isn’t sure that’s the case but she’s happy to see Chloe in such high spirits, her energy level improving. She even requests ice cream, which Rio fetches from the doctor’s lounge for her, just to make sure it’s the good stuff. 

Chloe’s renewed sense of energy starts to thaw the freezing feeling in Rio’s chest too. She can breathe a little deeper, think more clearly. 

Rio then finds a moment to get some charting done. But first, she steals a soda and graham crackers from the patient nourishment room, then settles into one of the physician computer stations lining the nurses’ station. She chats with a respiratory therapist about another patient, makes small talk about the weather with a student nurse. And 45 minutes later, most of her work is done and the day is looking like she might even be done with work early. Maybe she can sneak in dinner with Agatha at the hospital cafeteria; or her place if they have the time. 

Rio fetches her phone out of her white coat pocket and sends Agatha a text making plans for the evening. Agatha replies seconds later and soon they have plans for tacos and margaritas after work. 

Whatever feeling Rio thought she felt earlier must have been unexpected anxiety or exhaustion or…

The intercom suddenly crackles overhead, the sound echoing throughout the hallways. 

Code blue, room 1401. Code blue, room 1401.

Rio drops her pen, watching the plastic hitting the desk like it’s in slow motion. 

She feels her stomach drop, her heart beat tick up and her palms start to sweat just slightly. 

“Fuck! No, no, no.” Rio yells loud enough that several nurses turn around. “Fuck, it’s Chloe,” she lowers her voice, mumbling to no one in particular. 

She takes off down the hall, fast steps quickly turning into a full on run. She bangs through the door to the stairwell, taking them two at a time until she reaches the oncology floor.

The room is already packed with people - nurses, techs and laboratory personnel seeping onto the hallway. 

Rio pushes through the crowd, making her way deeper into the room. 

 

And for the first time in her career, Rio freezes. Standing there at the foot of the bed, she sees Chloe. Her small frame looks even smaller, swallowed whole by the bed beneath her. Her gown has been shoved haphazardly down her chest, the skin beneath it already blue and mottled. 

 

One of the nurses is frantically performing chest compressions, pounding against her ribs. Rio can hear small cracking noises heard as they snap beneath her palms. 

 

“Dr. Vidal,” somewhere she hears someone calling her name. “Dr. Vidal!” There is more yelling now and she snaps back into focus.

 

“Dr. Vidal! What do you want to do?” 

 

“Epi’s in?” Rio asks.

 

“Last round one minute ago,” a nurse calls from her position next to the crash cart. She checks the list in front of her where she has tracked all the medications given so far.  

“And has someone called Frank?” Rio asks into the crowd. 

“Who?” Comes the question from someone in the crowd.

“Her husband! Jesus, someone call her husband! Tell him to come right away. Don’t tell him she’s coding. Just get him here!” Rio can hear her voice fraying, her words coming out shakier than she intends.

The respiratory tech rhythmically squeezes the ambu bag. The plastic tube lodged deep in Chloe’s throat, breathing for her. Rio watches her chest rise and fall artificially. The motion is too stiff, too fake. 

“Pulse check,” she calls, her voice thin. 

Hands freeze. Silence falls over the room. 

Rio presses two fingers to Chloe’s carotid artery. A nurse rests a Doppler along her groin.

Nothing. 

Rio feels nothing but the vibration of her own pulse hammering back at her. 

She makes quick eye contact with the nurse and who shakes her head to confirm the same. 

“Resume compressions,” Rio commands.

For a brief second, the only sounds in the room are the near constant thump along Chloe’s chest, the silicone crinkle of the ambu bag. 

“What the hell happened?” Rio shouts to no one in particular. “She was fine this morning! She was fucking improving!” 

“I think it was the surge,” Rio turns to see Chloe’s nurse, eyes rimmed red. 

Fuck. The surge. How could she have overlooked that? That final rally, that burst of energy patients get right before they crash. Rio was so blinded by her fondness and compassion for Chloe, she never saw it coming. 

And now here she was, watching Chloe die in real time. 

“How long since the last epi?” Rio asks. 

“Two minutes.”

“Prep another 1mg then,” her lips form a thin line. “I want it given as soon as we hit three minutes from the last dose.” 

The drawers of the crash cart open and clang closed again. Trash litters the floor around them - saline flushes, syringe caps, gauze, plastic wrap. 

“Rio, it’s been 45 minutes already,” the charge nurse points out quietly. Rio tries not to notice the use of her first name; the attempt to appeal to the more human side of her. 

“Have we given bicarb yet?” Rio asks, ignoring the charge nurse’s insistence. 

“No,” another voice, maybe the pharmacist, points out. 

“Then give bicarb.”

Rio can feel the fatigue of the room. The audible exhales of several staff members. The way their motions are slower, their frantic state calmed just a bit. All of it screams one thing: we know it’s over and we are just going through the motions now.

But Rio isn’t done.

Not yet. 

“Push epi,” she calls out. 

“We’ve already given seven doses.”

“I. Don’t. Care.” Rio says through gritted teeth. “And where the hell is Frank?” She yells toward the door. 

She sees a chaplain stick his head in the doorway. “He’s ten minutes out.”

“Good.”

Deep down, Rio knows it’s over. But she isn’t ready to stop yet. 

More epinephrine. More compressions. 

They run out of medications in the crash cart and have to send an intern to run to another floor to grab more. Nursing students start taking over CPR as the nurses exhaust themselves. 

And then someone lets her know Frank is outside the door. 

Rio swallows hard, mentally preparing herself for what’s coming. 

She slows the room down. She excuses any staff not actively giving medications or CPR. She straightens the sheet over Chloe’s body, until only her chest - now an ugly grey-blue color - is visible. 

“Continue CPR,” Rio says quietly. 

And then she brings Frank in. To an outsider it seems cruel - letting the family watch those final moments. But it’s important. It not only lets him know they did everything they could, but it helps bring finality to those moments. 

His eyes are wide when he enters. Too wide. He walks slowly toward Chloe’s feet, hesitantly, unsure where to stand. 

Rio watches him take in the sight before him, the IV lines snaking out of her arms, plastic tube shoved down her throat, breathing for her. An exhausted nurse huddles over Chloe’s chest, compressing again and again. A futile effort to get her heart started again.

“Frank,” Rio starts carefully. “We’ve been trying for over an hour. Her body is too fragile.”

He doesn’t respond. He just watches them at work with a stunned, hollow expression.

“I’m afraid there is nothing more we can do,” she places a slow, careful hand on his shoulder. 

He doesn’t move. He doesn’t acknowledge her presence at all.

Rio meets the eyes of each member of her team. One by one. A silent consensus. She gives a subtle nod. They know what it means.

Everyone slowly withdrawals their hands. 

CPR stops.

The tech stops squeezing the ambu bag. 

They turn off the machines. 

The breaths stop. The beeping stops.

It’s quiet. 

Rio steps around Frank, placing her stethoscope in her ears. Her fingers tremble against her will.

She draws it up to Chloe’s chest, feeling the tears prick her eyes as she does.

She places it along Chloe’s ribs, where her heart is.

No sound comes back to her.

“Time of death: 15:28” she calls out. A slight pen scratch is heard as someone scribbles it down.

She walks back to Frank, ready to tell him to take his time saying goodbye. 

But he’s already moving. 

“No!” He suddenly yells. “That’s it? No, no, no!”

He runs to Chloe’s side. “You have to keep trying! You can’t give up like this!”

And then he places his own hands on her chest, frantically attempting CPR. His hands push desperately on her chest, sobs wracking his shoulders. 

No one else moves.

“Please,” he begs. “Someone help me please.” 

He keeps pushing. His moves are small, desperate. And useless. 

The staff doesn’t move. 

“Frank,” Rio murmurs, stepping closer. She places a hand on his arm, attempting to still his movements. 

“Dr. Vidal,” he chokes. “We have to keep going.”

“We tried,” she begins, her voice firm. “She’s dead.”

The word is brutal. It sounds harsh. She knows it does. But in that moment, she has to say the words.  Not “gone.” Not “in a better place.” Dead. He has to understand. It’s over. 

His head snaps toward her, his nostrils flare at her words.

“You said she was going to get better!” He shouts, jabbing a finger hard enough into her shoulder that she stumbles a bit. “You made promises like some kind of god!”

Rio sees a nurse step up, closer to her side, ready to defend her from Frank. Her hand shoots up to stop her. 

“I was hopeful Frank,” Rio says sternly, not backing down. “I never guaranteed anything.” 

“You’re not a saint, Doctor,” he spits. “You’re just an angel of Death!” 

And he collapses forward onto Chloe’s body, curling around her. He weeps into her gown, the noise loud and cruel. 

Rio steps back to give him space. Her team does the same.

No one says a word as they slip out of the room, closing the door behind them. 

Rio doesn’t stop to talk to her team. She doesn’t begin charting or go to the debrief. 

She just walks as fast as her feet will physically carry her - she cuts through the oncology wing, down the stairwell and out a side exit. The door slams behind her. 

The cold winter air instantly slaps her in the face. 

She finds herself in a back courtyard, hardly used and long since forgotten. Dead leaves pile in the corners. The plants are overgrown and tangled over the sidewalk. An old picnic table sits neglected in the center of it all, cracks broken through the benches. 

Rio presses her back to the brick wall of the hospital and exhales a long, shaky breath - then chokes on it, a sob ripping out before she can stop it. 

She cries for Chloe. 

She cries for Frank. 

She cries over the words he hurled at her - because they land too harsh, too truthful. 

She cries for herself because she couldn’t save anyone today. Not Chloe. Not Frank. And right now, not even herself. 

It must be ten minutes that Rio stands there. Maybe twenty. All she knows is she’s out there long enough that the wind cuts straight through her coat and scrubs, numbing her skin and stinging her eyes. For  a second, she thinks about how there must be a storm coming. Not that she cares. 

Instead she thinks about how she feels like she failed Chloe. How her body is being zipped into a transport bag, already on its way to the morgue. The morgue that is much colder than whatever Rio feels out here in the hospital courtyard.  

She wishes she had a cigarette right now. She’s regretting that she gave up the habit years ago. Maybe she should start keeping them in her white coat pocket for moments like this. Something to hold. Something to stop the trembling in her hands. 

Maybe it could keep the tears at bay. 

“Rio.” 

Agatha’s voice, cautious and small, threads through the cold air behind her. 

Rio doesn’t turn to face her. “How did you know where to find me?”

“I heard the overhead page. I figured you were sentimental enough to go to the same place I crashed out during my first code.”

Rio scoffs. 

“And Alice saw you,” Agatha adds. 

“That’s more like it,” Rio manages to muster up a soft smile as Agatha comes to stand beside her. Not touching. No crowding. Just there. A quiet, steady presence that she’s suddenly grateful for.  A grounding force. 

Agatha waits. Not asking. Not prying. Just giving her space to breathe without feeling alone.

And God - Rio could kiss her for it. Or fall apart for her. Or both. 

Instead, for now, she whispers, “Chloe fucking died.” The tears start to fall again, silently down her freezing cheeks. 

“Shit,” the way Agatha says it, it sounds like an apology. 

Rio nods, leaning back further into the wall until her head rests on the brick. 

Agatha scoots sideways until her shoulder is just brushing Rio’s. Her fingers reach out, wiping a tear that’s gathered along Rio’s jawline. 

“Rio?” Agatha asks, her voice small. “If Evanora would have approved the chemo, would she have lived?” 

“Yes.”

A beat.

“No.”

Rio wipes the remaining tears with the back of her head. Her voice is less shaky now. “I don’t know. It probably would have bought her more time. At least time to realize what was happening. Be more comfortable. Maybe even time to say goodbye.”

Rio can feel Agatha tense next to her. Her fists clenching and unclenching at her words.

“It’s like she did this to her,” Agatha grates. “Indirectly,” she continues. “But she still affected her life. And she doesn’t even know. She has no fucking idea.”

“She wouldn’t care if she did know,” Rio adds.

Agatha takes a long inhale, considering her words. “Yeah, you’re right,” she says finally. 

They stand like that. Shoulder to shoulder. Silent but soaking in each other’s presence just the same.

Agatha starts to shiver slightly next to her. She tugs her white coat closer around her, trying to ward off the cold. Out of the corner of her eye, Rio sees her look to the door a few times, hinting she wants to go inside. But she doesn’t make a move toward it. 

“Come ‘mere,” Rio opens her arms and Agatha settles into her chest. They both wrap their arms around each other - an embrace of warmth for Agatha, comfort for Rio. 

After a few minutes, Agatha mumbles into her shoulder, “Rio.” 

“Hmm?” Rio rests her cheek along Agatha’s hair. 

Agatha doesn’t pull back to meet her gaze, but Rio can feel her straightening her back, like she’s mustering up the courage to say something big. 

“We need to talk.”

Rio sucks in breath. “Fuck,” she mutters. She instantly drops her arms from Agatha’s shoulders and takes a step back. That’s not what she expected. It could not be a worse time for Agatha to come up with some relationship altering drama. And Rio doesn’t have the energy to fight her, not tonight. “Do we have to do this right now?”

Chapter End Notes

I’ve been planning Chloe’s death for a long time now - it serves so many purposes, some yet to be seen. I teared up writing this. It felt so raw to try to put into words what it feels like to watch your patient that you had much hope for, die. And even more to try to depict what it’s like to have to show the family what’s happening, to tell them it’s over. Frank’s reaction is all too common.

Also try to find the Taylor Swift lyric.
