He hops up from the kitchen table and grabs his backpack where it’s slung over the back of the chair by the door. He unzips it, rummaging around until he pulls out the thick folder and slaps it onto the table. 

Agatha and Rio lean forward. 

“How?” Rio asks, not wanting to finish the question.

“I stole them,” he says proudly. “Your straight and narrow fiance isn’t so straight after all.”

Agatha lets out a low whisper. “No way.” 

“Did you…” Agatha starts, wiggling her eyebrow. 

“Eww no,” Billy grimaces. “He’s totally not my type.”

Rio laughs. She doesn’t want to kill their vibe but, “I’m sure he has copies.” 

“Took care of that too.” 

Billy jumps up again, fishing something else ject from his backpack. 

“His laptop,” he presents proudly, dropping it on the table. 

Agatha’s chair scraps back suddenly, loud against the old wood floor. She disappears into the bedroom and shuts the door.  

Rio hesitates to follow her before…the crash makes her jump. 

Agatha is back, small hammer in her hand. She doesn’t hesitate. The blow caves the metal in, glass shattering beneath it. 

Agatha looks at Rio, her eyes wild and unhinged. “Looks like your present came in handy after all.”

She swings again. 

Rio doesn’t move to stop her. 

—

Two months. 

That’s all Agatha has left in his hell hole. 

After that, everything will be better. She keeps telling herself that. Like a promise. 

Agatha tells herself that as Jen drones on about sodium-potassium pumps and the role of activating medications. She throws her a snide comment about how she learned this in medical school and earns herself a scowl. 

She tells herself she’s almost free as Jen then makes her present a mini-lecture on diabetic medications and weight loss. When Jen asks her where she got her information, she tells her Rio taught her. She enjoys the flash of anger that crosses Jen’s face a little too much. 

And even though Rio hasn’t landed a job yet, Rio still reassured her, promised her that she’ll move anyway. Worst case scenario, she becomes a doc-in-box at the local Walgreens until she finds something more permanent. 

The point is, Rio and her will be together. Living in their own place. Exploring restaurants and parks in Boston on the weekends. Building something that belongs just to them. 

Agatha presses the elevator button, summoning it to the hospital lobby where she waits. 

It’s all Agatha can think about.

It’s all that keeps her going.

Right now, nothing can get her down.

Except…

“Agatha.” 

The elevator doors slide open to reveal her mother. 

Shit.

Agatha considers turning away and letting the doors close as she heads back toward the conference room. Pretend she never heard her name. 

“Agatha,” Evanora’s bony hand shoots out, stopping the doors. “I know you can hear me.” 

Agatha turns to plaster on her fakest smile. A pharmacy tech passes by, nodding toward them politely as he goes. 

She steps inside the elevator. At least here in the confines of these four walls, Evanora can berate her in private. 

“What are you even doing up here?” Agatha asks through gritted teeth. “I thought the hospital hallways were beneath you.”

“Oh they are. Filthy places,” Evanora looks around with open disgust. “But I heard you are moving.” 

Agatha draws a small breath, bracing herself. “Where did you hear that?” 

“Oh stupid girl. Don’t you know I know everything that goes on in my hospital?” Evanora gives a thin smile. “Including your move and your foolish attending running to follow you.” 

Agatha scoffs. “And here I thought you would be happy to be rid of me.” She reaches forward and presses a floor button - any floor. She doesn’t bother looking. She just wants off this ride.

Evanora shakes her head. “I wish I could be. But you are making this hospital, the residency, look bad. People keep asking me why we can’t even retain the CEO’s daughter.”

“Make up something,” Agatha snaps. “Tell them you kicked me out. I don’t care. I’m still leaving.”

The doors open and Agatha steps out as quickly as she can. 

She looks up just as Evanora’s smile turns to something sinister. 

“I’m thinking I might call…” Evanora snickers. “Boston is it?” 

The doors begin to close.

“I’m sure they would love to know what a gem of a resident they are getting.” 

“Fuck you,” Agatha says just as the doors seal shut. 

She stands there for a moment, staring at her reflection in the metal. 

Her eyes burn. Tears press close. She tries to blink them back but starts to fail. 

So she turns the opposite direction, down the hospital hallway. 

Her pager starts beeping almost immediately and Agatha ignores it. It’s probably Jen, harassing her about an admission. 

All she wants is Rio. 

To see her. To hold her. To cry about how much her mother hates her and how badly she wants to be done with this hospital - with all of it. 

Her pager buzzes again.

Then her cell phone. 

Damn, Jen is relentless today. 

She walks faster, head down, avoiding the nurses’ station until she spots a supply closet, a large one. She slips inside, moving all the way to the back, tucked between shelves of gauze and saline until she’s out of sight. 

Agatha sinks to the floor and folds in on herself, forehead resting on her knees. 

Her phone buzzes again. 

She tells herself she can ignore it for a minute more. Just until the nausea fades and the anger passes enough for her to breathe normally again. 

She can hear the hospital chaos outside the walls. Someone shouts, a metal tray clangs to the ground, a door slams. Footsteps rush past the supply closet door but it never opens. 

Good. Let them deal with the mayhem; she just needs quiet. 

Her pager buzzes again. 

She huffs, blowing out her cheeks in frustration. 

So much for finding peace. 

With an exacerbated sigh, she pulls the pager from her white coat pocket, ready to fling it across the room. 

Instead, she looks down. 

Not Jen.

A hospital wide message. 

 

Code silver.

 

She mentally runs through the list of codes: code blue, code pink, code yellow. She can’t recall a code silver.

She grabs her cell phone to look it up and instead finds a flood of messages from Rio: 

 

Agatha

Agatha! 

Where are you?

What floor are you on? 

Are you safe?

Answer your phone! 

Dammit Agatha, answer me now! 

FUCK AGATHA PLEASE  

 

Her breath catches. 

Her phone starts ringing immediately. 

She answers on instinct, forcing a thin, shaky laugh. But inside her heart is racing. Something feels wrong. The noises outside the closet are louder now, more frantic. 

“What’s so important that you had to text me so many times?” She tries to sound casual, hoping the frenzy is just manufactured in her head. 

“Agatha,” Rio says her name like a prayer, full of tension and pleading. She whispers into the speaker, “Are you ok? Are you safe?”

“Of course I am,” Agatha says automatically. “What’s going on? Why are you whispering?”

“Where are you?” Rio presses. “What floor are you on?”

Agatha freezes and looks around the supply closet. Identical shelves as every other floor. No windows. No signage. 

“I…I don’t know,” she admits. “I hit a random elevator button. I didn’t even look.” 

On the other end of the line, Rio goes very still.

“Okay,” Rio whispers. Agatha can hear the shaking in her voice. “Listen to me, don’t leave that room.”

Agatha scoots backward until her shoulders hit the wall. 

Another sound filters through the ceiling - a sharp pop, like fireworks, muffled as it comes from another floor. 

Still it makes her flinch. 

“You’re starting to scare me, Rio,” she says quietly. “What is a Code Silver? Like…a mass casualty?”  

“No.” Rio swallows hard enough that Agatha can hear it through the phone.

“There’s a gunman in the hospital.” 

—

Chapter End Notes

Here. We. Go.

Chapter 24: Xenial

Chapter Notes

Trigger warnings for extreme gun violence, blood, gunshot wounds. .

See the end of the chapter for more notes

The day started out like any other.

That’s always how it is, isn’t it?

The worst day of your life never starts out the worst. It starts out normally - bitter coffee, stale pastries and bright, fluorescent overhead lights. 

Rio’s rounds run long. A patient’s potassium is low for seemingly no reason and she orders the replacement - which they promptly refuse to take. A nurse flags her down to ask about a patient who looks fine but doesn’t feel right, Rio spends an extra 20 minutes in their room checking and rechecking until she’s satisfied. 

She signs three patient charts, orders about 50 labs and jokes with a resident about how the cafeteria somehow made the eggs worse. 

That’s the last moment that her day, her life, will ever be normal again. 

Rio is in a patient’s room, leaning back against the counter while a sweet, elderly woman explains why she didn’t think potato chips counted against her low-salt heart failure diet. It’s then that her pager, clipped to her scrub pants, starts beeping. 

She silences it, as she usually does, content on checking the message later. 

It beeps again. 

Rio purses her lips, before finishing her sentence and glancing down, already half-expecting a medication question or a family request. 

Instead, the screen glows with two words. 

Code Silver

Her blood turns to ice in her veins. That…that can’t be right, can it? It has to be a drill, an error. Anything else.

As soon as the noise starts outside the patient room, she knows the rest of the hospital heard it too. Doors slam shut, locks clicking. Patient beds are pulled away from windows. Lights are turned off. 

Without a word, she smiles sweetly at her patient, walking to close the blinds of her room. 

“What’s going on?” Her patient asks, hearing the commotion. 

“Just a drill, ma’am,” Rio is calm, steady. She doesn’t shake. 

Until, Agatha. 

The thought hits so hard, it almost knocks the air out of her lungs. Nausea comes at her like a wave crashing to shore as she realizes she doesn’t know where Agatha is or what she’s doing. 

She pulls out her phone, thumbing a quick message to ease her fears.

Agatha.

She presses send. She waits less than a minute to send a second text. 

Agatha! 

Where are you?

No reply. Her heartbeat picks up a bit. 

What floor are you on?

She’s just busy, she reassures herself. And hasn’t seen her pager. 

Are you safe?

Answer your phone! 

When there is still no response, her throat starts to feel tight, her heart rate too fast.

Dammit Agatha, answer me now! 

FUCK AGATHA PLEASE 

Fuck it, she’s going to call her. 

“What’s so important that you had to text me so many times?” Agatha answers immediately. Rio knows her well enough to recognize fake bravado. 

“Agatha,” Rio pleads. Her voice drops to a whisper, trying not to scare the patient in front of her. “Are you ok? Are you safe?”

“Of course I am,” Agatha responds. “What’s going on? Why are you whispering?”

Agatha doesn’t know. At least that means she’s safe, unaffected by whatever prompted the code. 

“Where are you?” Rio presses. “What floor are you on?”

Rio doesn’t get a response. Not immediately anyway. She can hear Agatha shuffling around on the other end of the line. 

“I…I don’t know,” Agatha finally says. “I hit a random elevator button. I didn’t even look.” 

A chill runs through Rio. That could mean anything. She could be as close as the supply room down the hall or as far away as four floors. 

“Okay,” Rio whispers. She hears the tremor in her own voice this time and doesn’t bother hiding it. “Listen to me, don’t leave that room.”

A distant pop rattles through the phone, causing Agatha to gasp. Rio freezes, listening for the sound on her end. Nothing. Her floor remains silent - so they aren’t in the same place.

“You’re starting to scare me,” Agatha says quietly. “What is a Code Silver? Like…a mass casualty?”  

“No.” The nausea is mounting now, bile rising in her throat. “There’s a gunman in the hospital.”

“I…” Agatha starts, then stops. Her breathing comes more rapidly through the speaker now, voice shaking.

Rio can’t sit idly by, hoping a phone call is enough to sustain them both through this ordeal. 

She has to protect her, she has to shield her. She has to…

She has to find her. 

“Listen to me,” Rio says. “I need you to stay low. Crawl if you have to. Go to the door and just barely crack it. You need to tell me what floor you are on.”

A shaky breath on the other line. “Ok, ok. I can do that.” Rio hears movement on the other end. Then a pause.

“Rio?”

“I’m here.”

“I can’t crawl and hold the phone. I have to set it down.”

“Don’t hang up,” Rio says immediately. “Just leave it on. I’ll stay.” 

Time stretches on for what feels like an eternity. Every nerve in her body feels exposed, flayed open like she’s the one on the operating table this time. 

Rio takes the time to pull a chair closer to the patient’s bed and leans down. 

“Listen to me very carefully,” she whispers. “There is an active shooter in the hospital. I don’t know where. I don’t know who.”

The woman’s eyes widen, terror blooming across her features.

“If anyone comes in this room,” Rio continues, “you do not move. You lie every still. You play dead. Do you understand me?”

She nods slowly. Her trembling hands clutch the blanket around her. “I have to call my family…” 

“Do what you need to do as quietly as possible.” 

The phone crackles again with Agatha’s voice. “Rio?”

Oh thank God.

“I’m here,” Rio sighs in relief. “I’m here Agatha.”

“I’m on the third floor.” 

She’s two floors below her. Rio can’t risk the elevator, it’s likely locked down by now anyway. Main stairwells will be locked as well.

But the back stairwell, the one they use to access the sixth floor - that one might be their saving grace. 

Rio exhales. “It’s going to be ok.” She doesn’t know that.

“We’re going to be ok,” she continues. She doesn’t know that either.

Rio knows the rules, she’s been through the training. Stay put, secure the unit, reassure the patients. 

She doesn’t care. 

Rio eases toward the door, peering through the narrow window. The units is so still - the lights are low, staff huddled in back rooms and closets where they hide silently. 

She can’t sit here idly and wait. 

“Dr. Vidal?” Her patient whispers from behind her. “What are you going to do?”

“I’m going out there. I have to save someone.” 

Rio’s hands start sweating as she eases the door open. She slips only her head out, scanning the hallway inch by inch. 

Nothing. 

It’s eerie actually. 

The hallway is dim, the only light now filtering through the windows from the outside. 

She slips out the door, pressing her back to the wall. The purpose is two-fold: to become smaller, less of a target and to give herself a chance to attempt to calm.

Her heart is pounding so hard, she swears she can hear her pulse in her ears. Her breathing is erratic - too fast and she risks hyperventilation just standing here. 

She squeezes her eyes shut, risking a moment of darkness behind her eyelids in an attempt to not allow her own body to give her away.

Breath in - 1, 2, 3, 4. 

Hold - 1, 2, 3, 4. 

Breath out - 1, 2, 3, 4 

As she slows, one thing becomes more apparent. Not a sound can be heard on the entire floor. 

There is no beeping of monitors, clicking of keyboards, or doors opening and closing. Gone are the near constant conversations and movement of people in and out. 

If she didn’t know any better, it would simply feel like the middle of a night shift. Like the world is fast asleep around her. 

Against her better judgement, Rio bends and slips off her sneakers, setting them down slowly on the floor. She pads down the hallway toward the stairwell exit sign in her socked feet. Her footsteps are now silent. 

Just before the door, she pauses, hand poised on the handle. 

She listens.

No sound comes from the other side. 

She eases the door open. It gives a soft click, still far too loud in her ears and she slips inside, pulling it closed just as carefully. 

The stairwell is even darker than the hall - no windows or lights to illuminate the concrete that she now descends. She takes each steps tentatively, listening, assessing as best she can as she moves. 

She has no idea where the gunman is. Or who it is. She assumes the cops or swat are on their way. Perhaps the entire time is close to being resolved already.

No such luck. As she descends to the last step - her foot slides. She hits something slick, pitching forward. Her heart lurches, adrenaline feeling like it suddenly shoots through her. Her fingers reach out blindly, grabbing the railing just before she hits the ground. 

Her socks are wet. Warm. 

She looks down. 

Blood pools beneath her, spreading slowly across the concrete. It seeps into the fabric of her socks, clinging to her skin. 

She doesn’t want to look up. She already knows nothing good awaits her. 

But Rio forces her gaze anyway. 

Alice. 

She’s slumped over against the wall, head hanging low. Dark blood, almost black, saturates the concrete beneath her. The sticky mess isn’t cake onto the floor or drying in the cool air - it’s new. Fresh. 

“No, no. Please God,” Rio chokes on her own words. She slaps a hand over her mouth, trying to muffle the scream that threatens to escape. 

Hot, wet tears blur her vision. A mix of anger and overwhelming grief. But she forces herself to bend down to check for a pulse.

Faint. Thready. But there. There is skin warm to the touch, beneath her fingertips. 

“Alice, talk to me honey. Where were you hit?”

“Arm,” comes her hoarse whisper.  

Rio grasps the left shoulder of Alice’s white coat, now saturated with blood. And she rips. The wet fabric falls away. Underneath is a clear wound, still oozy a large amount of blood. Rio carefully lifts Alice’s arm to inspect it. 

The pain shoots through Alice and she lets out a gut-wrenching cry. 

In that instant, a sound echoes above them. Or maybe below them. Rio’s ears deceive her and she can’t tell if it’s the building groaning or footsteps heading closer. She thinks she hears sirens in the distance, but maybe it’s just wishful thinking. 

The tension has Rio’s body locking up, betraying her where she sits. Involuntary shaking starts takes over - her hands, her arms, even her teeth chatter uncontrollably. 

Fuck. 

She sees her fingers shaking where she holds Alice’s arm. 

“I have…to see…if the…the bullet is still…there,” her words come out broken behind chattering teeth. Rio purses her lips, trying to will herself to stop shaking. “You cannot…scream. No matter how much it hurts.” 

Rio takes her non-reply as understanding. She lifts Alice’s arm carefully to inspect the backside. 

Alice breaks out into silent sobs, mouth opening in a scream, but she remains silent.

For the first time today, Rio feels relieved. “It’s…it’s ok. It’s through-and-through,” Rio explains. “But I have to move you. Get pressure on the wound. You’ve lost too much blood.”

Alice just groans in response. 

Rio hooks her hands around Alice’s waist, heaving her over her shoulder. Where she would normally be steady, lifting with ease, her knees now feel weak, threatening to buckle below her. 

Her hands yank at the third floor door. It slams behind her, the sound echoing through the once silent building. It makes her wince. 

She finds an empty patient room, a bed neatly made before her. She deposits Alice onto it as carefully as she can in her weak state. Blood still seeps from the wound, not fast but steady enough to soak the sheets. 

Rio rummages through the cabinets and drawers in the room to find them all empty. Fucking hospital regulations. 

Alice needs a tourniquet. 

Electric cords slip too much to form tight knots. An empty room means no readily available IV tubing. Rio attempts to rip a strip of fabric from the bedding below Alice. But re-enforced edges and her unsteady, shaking hands means she’s unsuccessful. 

A shoelace would work perfectly. 

And Rio’s shoes were sitting two floors above her, the laces untied.

She looks down at Alice’s shoes. Slip-ons.

“I’m going to find some supplies,” Rio says roughly. Her hands are still trembling. The rushes of adrenaline are starting to make her feel ill - a headache throbs in her temples and behind her eyes, dizziness threatening to overtake her. 

She steps out of the room and once again presses herself flat into the wall. 

A harsh crack splits through the air. The sound is piercing. It causes Rio to jump, fear like she’s never felt in her life surging through her. Ringing starts in Rio’s ears almost instantly. The smell of remnants of gunsmoke fill the hall. 

It’s close. 

So close.

Another surge of dread and adrenaline rockets through her at the possibility that it could have been aimed at Agatha. She feels like crumbling, right there in the hallway at the possibility that she could be somewhere on this floor - alone, injured and dying. 

She rounds the corner and nearly collides with a nurse. They both gasp and recoil. The nurse pivots instantly to flee, but Rio snags the edge of her scrubs with her fingertips.

“Hey, hey it’s ok,” Rio pleads. “I need your help,” 

The nurse nods wildly, her eyes wide with terror. 

Rio points to Alice’s room. “A doctor has been hit. Tourniquet her left arm and start on IV in the right. Pump her full of fluids until someone can get to you.” 

The nurse freezes, the words not registering. 

“Go!” Rio whispers harshly. 

The nurse bolts for a nearby supply cart, easing drawers open with shaking hands, moving as quietly as her fear will allow. 

Rio turns away before she can second guess herself. She hopes Alice will forgive her for leaving. That they will both be alive to have that conversation. 

For now, she has to find Agatha. 

Rio continues down the hallway, her bloody socks leaving wet footprints in her wake. She peels them off mid-stride, shoving them into her pocket and continues in her bare feet.

There are at least 3 supply closets on each floor. And Agatha gave her no indication of which one she was in. Rio isn’t even sure Agatha knows. It’s a blind guess. 

Would Agatha run into the first one she sees or go all the way to the end of the hall, away from people? She doesn’t have time to try to mentally untangle Agatha’s instinct. She reaches for the handle of the first door she comes to. 

She imagines Agatha sitting in the back corner, legs drawn up, waiting for her. 

They can huddle in there together, behind the shelves, out of sight and ride this thing out. 

They will be so hidden, so hard to find. 

She yanks open the door. 

It’s not Agatha that greets her on the other side. 

“Dr. Vidal,” a man’s voice snickers, lips curling cruelly over his teeth. “Just the person I was looking for.”

“Frank!” She squeaks louder than she intended, the name cracking in her throat. “I…”

Rio tumbles backward out the door, bare feet tangling as she falls onto the linoleum floor. Her ass hits hard enough to bruise her tailbone, but it’s of little concern now. 

She doesn’t have time to stand because Frank starts stalking toward her. Even in the near darkness of the hallway, she can see the shiny metal in his right hand, fingers wrapped around the trigger. 

She scrambles backward, flipping over to crawl on her hands and knees as fast as she can, but Frank is faster. She feels a hand on her ankle before she’s yanked across the cool floor toward him. 

“YOU,” he roars. With one hand still on her ankle, he flips her over until she faces him. She lifts her back quickly off the floor, feet flat on the floor, knees bent. It’s too vulnerable.

His right hand lifts. 

And suddenly, from her spot on the floor, Rio is staring down the barrel of his gun. 

“You killed my wife.” 

The cold steel presses between her eyes, biting into the skin of her forehead. 

This is it. This is how it ends. 

They say when Death is coming for you, you can feel it. There is no playback of happy moments, no reel flashing before your eyes. Time slows. A sixth sense that when the great beyond is headed for you, you know it. 

That Death herself is waiting, watching from the corner of the room to usher you to the other side. 

Rio feels it now. Like she’s standing on the edge of something, her toes leaning dangerously over the edge. The hallway around her dims, the edges of her vision blurring, tunneling inward until there’s nothing left but what’s directly in front of her. Frank. The gun. Like sinking into oblivion. Like being pulled underwater in the ocean, the deep dark closing in with no room to turn back or swim up. 

There was a time when Rio believed in God. She sat on hard wooden pews every Sunday, velvet dresses sliding along the varnish. Her mother would be beside her, faithfully tracing the sign of the cross. Rio would press her knees into wooden kneelers until they ached, trying to atone for sins she didn’t know she committed. When she turned seven, she donned the frilly white dress, flowers in her hair while communion was placed on her tongue. 

She no longer believes in God. 

When the church told her she would go to hell simply for falling in love with the wrong gender, she couldn’t justify the devotion anymore. 

Now on her knees, she whispers prayers anyway - not to God, not really. To anything. To everything. Something that might reach out and keep her alive. 

Something wet slides down her cheeks. It takes her a second to realize she’s crying. 

Frank is shouting now. Her name. His wife’s name. The words are swirling together, muffling as they reach her ears until she can’t make them out anymore. Grief, blame, heartache consuming him; rushing toward her. 

It doesn’t matter what he says. Not really. Because the end is coming at her like a freight train and she’s helpless to stop it. 

The sound of footsteps coming toward them startles them both. 

Frank swings blindly toward the sound, firing twice. One round cracks into a wall. The other sparks off the floor. 

Then a figure comes to stand in the hallway in the haze of the gunsmoke. Blue scrubs, unruly hair. 

Even without a clear view of her face, Rio knows exactly who it is. 

“No, no. Please Agatha!” Rio begs, panic tearing from her chest. She lifts a hand, frantic as if she could physically wave her away by magic. “Agatha, you have to go! You have to leave right now.” 

“Shut up!” Frank shouts, whipping the gun back toward Rio. “Just shut up! I can’t think when you are hysterical like that.” 

“I’m not leaving you,” Agatha says defiantly, ignoring Frank completely.

But even from this distance, Rio can see it - and it means Frank must too. There is a tremor in Agatha’s hands, her breathing shallow and stuttered. Tears are already streaking down her face, dark tracks down her cheeks from her mascara. 

Agatha takes a step toward them.

“Stop!” Frank shouts, snapping the gun in her direction.

Agatha freezes. Slowly, she lifts her hands in surrender. But her eyes never leave his - she narrows her gaze at him with confidence she doesn’t actually have. 

She’s baiting him. 

Rio’s stomach tightens at the realization - Agatha isn’t trying to escape. 

She is offering herself, walking into death on purpose. 

Frank swipes a hand across his face, exhaling raggedly. His shoulders tense, the barrel wavering in his grip. He’s losing control - and that might be the worst case scenario. 

The second he looks away, just a fraction of an inch, Agatha steps forward again. 

“I said STOP!” he roars. 

Her lips curve faintly, just enough to try to show defiance, not fear. Rio hates that she sees right through it. The way Agatha’s lip trembles, the way her hands shake slightly where they are raised, the red of her eyes - despite looking death in the face, Agatha is terrified. 

“You are trying to distract me from her,” he snaps. His patience is fraying. The gun swings wildly now, back and forth between them.

“Frank, ignore her,” Rio starts, more steady than she feels. “I’m right here. It’s me you want.”

Frank lets out a humorless, cruel laugh. 

Agatha doesn’t back down. “Please. Just put the gun down.” 

“I said stop talking!” Frank’s anger boils over, red blotches covering his cheeks and chest now, beads of sweat form along his brow. “You don’t get to talk.” 

He jabs the gun toward Rio. “You think this ends with her saving you?” 

Rio shakes her head wildly. She focuses only on Frank. Avoiding eye contact with Agatha completely. “I didn’t ask her to. She’s nothing. Nobody. It’s just you and me, Frank. Focus on me.” She hopes Frank doesn’t see through the lie. She hopes Agatha does.  

“Oh but that’s where you are wrong. Because you are going to pay for her little mistake.”

“Wait…” Rio barely gets the word out before the butt of the gun collides with her temple. 

White bursts behind her eyes as her head snaps back. Instantly, she tastes blood. The roaring in her ears is back, louder than before.

Through the haze, Agatha screams. She lunges forward two steps before she’s stopped again. 

“Don’t move!” Frank screams, whipping the gun back up. “Don’t you dare move again.”

Rio tries to blink the hallway back into focus. Her head spins when she turns toward Frank. 

He’s breathing too hard, too erratic as his chest heaves. He looks…almost scared. 

“This isn’t about you,” he yells down the hall toward Agatha. She’s made it halfway to them already. Rio wants to yell for her to back up, but she can’t risk provoking Frank further. “This is between us.” 

The barrel of the gun is back, aimed directly at her forehead. But this time, Rio looks past him. She shakes her head at Agatha, just barely. 

Because Rio knows the truth - there is no plan, no leverage. There is no way out. 

She sees Agatha’s face fall, the horror flickering across her features. Her eyes go glassy. She understands it too. This is the moment. They’ve run out of time. 

“I love you,” Rio mouths. 

Rio doesn’t close her eyes. She locks them against Agatha’s - her blue eyes swirling like a storm meet her deep brown. 

She wants her last sight to be Agatha’s face. To make sure she knows. 

“I love you too,” Agatha whispers. Then her hands twitch slightly, curling into fists where she drops them to her sides. She straightens her spine. 

The gun clicks as it cocks. 

And just before Rio closes her eyes, she sees Agatha move - breaking into a run, straight toward her.

Toward the gun.

And then…

A loud bang erupts, echoing in the confined space.
